## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship of a material. Stress typically increases with strain (elastic/hardening behavior) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), with possible Arrhenius-type thermal activation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (strain hardening in plastic regime)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with Arrhenius thermal term)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress and hardening)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (hardening with power-law thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Zener-Hollomon inspired: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (hyperbolic sine flow stress law)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined linear and nonlinear strain terms)
- Combined hardening-softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Swift-Voce hybrid: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with exponential thermal term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening with diminishing rate → Power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturating forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Modulus term multiplied by decreasing function of T: (c0 + c1*T) with c1<0, or exp(c*T) with c<0
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) where T is absolute temperature, indicating energy barrier controlled deformation
- Yield stress plus hardening → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) structure, where c0 represents initial yield stress
- Multiplicative decomposition of effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable strain hardening and thermal softening functions
- Hyperbolic sine stress law → sinh or asinh functions arise from forward-backward thermal activation (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart model)
- Strain-temperature coupling → At higher temperatures, hardening exponent or rate may change, suggesting T-dependent exponents like epsilon**(c0 + c1*T)
- Negative temperature sensitivity → Flow stress decreasing with T suggests thermal softening; steeper decrease at high T suggests exponential or power-law decay in T
